reused to save allocations.\n// GetGauge, GetCounter, etc are also cached, which means GetGauge will work for counter\n// if previously gauge was parsed. It's up to the caller to use Type to decide what\n// method to use when checking the value.\n//\n// TODO(bwplotka): io.Reader approach is possible too, but textparse has access to whole scrape for now.\nfunc NewMetricStreamingDecoder(data []byte) *MetricStreamingDecoder {\n\treturn &MetricStreamingDecoder{\n\t\tin:           data,\n\t\tMetricFamily: &MetricFamily{},\n\t\tMetric:       &Metric{},\n\t\tmetrics:      make([]pos, 0, 100),\n\t}\n}\n\nvar errInvalidVarint = errors.New(\"clientpb: invalid varint encountered\")\n\n// NextMetricFamily decodes the next metric family from the input without metrics.\n// Use NextMetric() to decode metrics. The MetricFamily fields Name, Help and Unit\n// are only valid until NextMetricFamily is called again.\nfunc (m *MetricStreamingDecoder) NextMetricFamily() error {\n\tb := m.in[m.inPos:]\n\tif len(b) == 0 {\n\t\treturn io.EOF\n\t}\n\tmessageLength, varIntLength := proto.DecodeVarint(b) // TODO(bwplotka): Get rid of gogo.\n\tif varIntLength == 0 || varIntLength > binary.MaxVarintLen32 {\n\t\treturn errInvalidVarint\n\t}\n\ttotalLength := varIntLength + int(messageLength)\n\tif totalLength > len(b) {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"clientpb: insufficient length of buffer, expected at least %d bytes, got %d bytes\", totalLength, len(b))\n\t}\n\tm.resetMetricFamily()\n\tm.mfData = b[varIntLength:totalLength]\n\n\tm.inPos += totalLength\n\treturn m.unmarshalWithoutMetrics(m, m.mfData)\n}\n\n// resetMetricFamily resets all the fields in m to equal the zero value, but re-using slice memory.\nfunc (m *MetricStreamingDecoder) resetMetricFamily() {\n\tm.metrics = m.metrics[:0]\n\tm.metricIndex = 0\n\tm.MetricFamily.Reset()\n}\n\nfunc (m *MetricStreamingDecoder) NextMetric() error {\n\tif m.metricIndex >= len(m.metrics) {\n\t\treturn io.EOF\n\t}\n\n\tm.resetMetric()\n\tm.mData = m.mfData[m.metrics[m.metricIndex].start:m.metrics[m.metricIndex].end]\n\tif err := m.unmarshalWithoutLabels(m, m.mData); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tm.metricIndex++\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// resetMetric resets all the fields in m to equal the zero value, but re-using slices memory.\nfunc (m *MetricStreamingDecoder) resetMetric() {\n\tm.labels = m.labels[:0]\n\tm.TimestampMs = 0\n\n\t// TODO(bwplotka): Autogenerate reset functions.\n\tif m.Counter != nil {\n\t\tm.Counter.Value = 0\n\t\tm.Counter.CreatedTimestamp = nil\n\t\tm.Counter.Exemplar = nil\n\t}\n\tif m.Gauge != nil {\n\t\tm.Gauge.Value = 0\n\t}\n\tif m.Histogram != nil {\n\t\tm.Histogram.SampleCount = 0\n\t\tm.Histogram.SampleCountFloat = 0\n\t\tm.Histogram.SampleSum = 0\n\t\tm.Histogram.Bucket = m.Histogram.Bucket[:0]\n\t\tm.Histogram.CreatedTimestamp = nil\n\t\tm.Histogram.Schema = 0\n\t\tm.Histogram.ZeroThreshold = 0\n\t\tm.Histogram.ZeroCount = 0\n\t\tm.Histogram.ZeroCountFloat = 0\n\t\tm.Histogram.NegativeSpan = m.Histogram.NegativeSpan[:0]\n\t\tm.Histogram.NegativeDelta = m.Histogram.NegativeDelta[:0]\n\t\tm.Histogram.NegativeCount = m.Histogram.NegativeCount[:0]\n\t\tm.Histogram.PositiveSpan = m.Histogram.PositiveSpan[:0]\n\t\tm.Histogram.PositiveDelta = m.Histogram.PositiveDelta[:0]\n\t\tm.Histogram.PositiveCount = m.Histogram.PositiveCount[:0]\n\t\tm.Histogram.Exemplars = m.Histogram.Exemplars[:0]\n\t}\n\tif m.Summary != nil {\n\t\tm.Summary.SampleCount = 0\n\t\tm.Summary.SampleSum = 0\n\t\tm.Summary.Quantile = m.Summary.Quantile[:0]\n\t\tm.Summary.CreatedTimestamp = nil\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (*MetricStreamingDecoder) GetMetric() {\n\tpanic(\"don't use GetMetric, use Metric directly\")\n}\n\nfunc (*MetricStreamingDecoder) GetLabel() {\n\tpanic(\"don't use GetLabel, use Label instead\")\n}\n\n// unsafeLabelAdder adds labels for a single metric.\n// The \"unsafe\" word highlights that some strings must not be retained on a\n// caller side. When used with labels.ScratchBuilder ensure it's used\n// with SetUnsafeAdd set to true.\ntype unsafeLabelAdder interface {\n\tAdd(name, value string)\n}\n\n// Label parses labels into unsafeLabelAdder. Metric name is missing\n// given the protobuf metric model and has to be deduced from the metric family name.\n//\n// TODO: The Label method name intentionally hide MetricStreamingDecoder.Metric.Label\n// field to avoid direct use (it's not parsed). However, with the\n    35→// type-and-unit-label feature (PROM-39), this information can be now stored directly\n    36→// in the special schema metadata labels, which offers better reliability (e.g. atomicity),\n    37→// compatibility and, in many cases, efficiency.\n    38→//\n    39→// NOTE: Metadata in the current form is generally similar (yet different) to:\n    40→//   - The MetricFamily definition in OpenMetrics (https://prometheus.io/docs/specs/om/open_metrics_spec/#metricfamily).\n    41→//     However, there is a small and important distinction around the metric name semantics\n    42→//     for the \"classic\" representation of complex metrics like histograms. The\n    43→//     Metadata.Name follows the __name__ semantics. See Name for details.\n    44→//   - Original metadata.Metadata entries. However, not all fields in that metadata\n    45→//     are \"identifiable\", notably the help field, plus metadata does not contain Name.\n    46→type Metadata struct {\n    47→\t// Name represents the final metric name for a Prometheus series.\n    48→\t// NOTE(bwplotka): Prometheus scrape formats (e.g. OpenMetrics) define\n    49→\t// the \"metric family name\". The Metadata.Name (so __name__ label) is not\n    50→\t// always the same as the MetricFamily.Name e.g.:\n    51→\t// * OpenMetrics metric family name on scrape: \"acme_http_router_request_seconds\"\n    52→\t// * Resulting Prometheus metric name: \"acme_http_router_request_seconds_sum\"\n    53→\t//\n    54→\t// Empty string means nameless metric (e.g. result of the PromQL function).\n    55→\tName string\n    56→\t// Type represents the metric type. Empty value (\"\") is equivalent to\n    57→\t// model.UnknownMetricType.\n    58→\tType model.MetricType\n    59→\t// Unit represents the metric unit. Empty string means an unitless metric (e.g.\n    60→\t// result of the PromQL function).\n    61→\t//\n    62→\t// NOTE: Currently unit value is not strictly defined other than OpenMetrics\n    63→\t// recommendations: https://prometheus.io/docs/specs/om/open_metrics_spec/#units-and-base-units\n    64→\t// TODO(bwplotka): Consider a stricter validation and rules e.g. lowercase only or UCUM standard.\n    65→\t// Read more in https://github.com/prometheus/proposals/blob/main/proposals/2024-09-25_metadata-labels.md#more-strict-unit-and-type-value-definition\n    66→\tUnit string\n    67→}\n    68→\n    69→// NewMetadataFromLabels returns the schema metadata from the labels.\n    70→func NewMetadataFromLabels(ls labels.Labels) Metadata {\n    71→\ttyp := model.MetricTypeUnknown\n    72→\tif got := ls.Get(model.MetricTypeLabel); got != \"\" {\n    73→\t\ttyp = model.MetricType(got)\n    74→\t}\n    75→\treturn Metadata{\n    76→\t\tName: ls.Get(model.MetricNameLabel),\n    77→\t\tType: typ,\n    78→\t\tUnit: ls.Get(model.MetricUnitLabel),\n    79→\t}\n    80→}\n    81→\n    82→// IsTypeEmpty returns true if the metric type is empty (not set).\n    83→func (m Metadata) IsTypeEmpty() bool {\n    84→\treturn m.Type == \"\" || m.Type == model.MetricTypeUnknown\n    85→}\n    86→\n    87→// IsEmptyFor returns true if the Metadata field, represented by the given labelName\n    88→// is empty (not set). If the labelName in not representing any Metadata field,\n    89→// IsEmptyFor returns true.\n    90→func (m Metadata) IsEmptyFor(labelName string) bool {\n    91→\tswitch labelName {\n    92→\tcase model.MetricNameLabel:\n    93→\t\treturn m.Name == \"\"\n    94→\tcase model.MetricTypeLabel:\n    95→\t\treturn m.IsTypeEmpty()\n    96→\tcase model.MetricUnitLabel:\n    97→\t\treturn m.Unit == \"\"\n    98→\tdefault:\n    99→\t\treturn true\n   100→\t}\n   101→}\n   102→\n   103→// AddToLabels adds metric schema metadata as labels into the labels.ScratchBuilder.\n   104→// Empty Metadata fields will be ignored (not added).\n   105→func (m Metadata) AddToLabels(b *labels.ScratchBuilder) {\n   106→\tif m.Name != \"\" {\n   107→\t\tb.Add(model.MetricNameLabel, m.Name)\n   108→\t}\n   109→\tif !m.IsTypeEmpty() {\n   110→\t\tb.Add(model.MetricTypeLabel, string(m.Type))\n   111→\t}\n   112→\tif m.Unit != \"\" {\n   113→\t\tb.Add(model.MetricUnitLabel, m.Unit)\n   114→\t}\n   115→}\n   116→\n   117→// SetToLabels injects metric schema metadata as labels into the labels.Builder.\n   118→// It follows the labels.Builder.Set semantics, so empty Metadata fields will\n   119→// remove the corresponding existing labels if they were previously set.\n   120→func (m Metadata) SetToLabels(b *labels.Builder) {\n   121→\tb.Set(model.MetricNameLabel, m.Name)\n   122→\tif m.Type == model.MetricTypeUnknown {\n   123→\t\t// Unknown equals empty semantically, so remove the label on unknown too as per\n   124→\t\t// method signature comment.\n   125→\t\tb.Set(model.MetricTypeLabel, \"\")\n   126→\t} else {\n   127→\t\tb.Set(model.MetricTypeLabel, string(m.Type))\n   128→\t}\n   129→\tb.Set(model.MetricUnitLabel, m.Unit)\n   130→}\n   131→\n   132→// NewIgnoreOverriddenMetadataLabelScratchBuilder creates IgnoreOverriddenMetadataLabelScratchBuilder.\n   133→func (m Metadata) NewIgnoreOverriddenMetadataLabelScratchBuilder(b *labels.ScratchBuilder) *IgnoreOverriddenMetadataLabelScratchBuilder {\n   134→\treturn &IgnoreOverriddenMetadataLabelScratchBuilder{ScratchBuilder: b, overwrite: m}\n   135→}\n   136→\n   137→// IgnoreOverriddenMetadataLabelScratchBuilder is a wrapper over labels.ScratchBuilder\n   138→// that ignores label additions that would collide with non-empty Overwrite Metadata fields.\n   139→type IgnoreOverriddenMetadataLabelScratchBuilder struct {\n   140→\t*labels.ScratchBuilder\n   141→\toverwrite Metadata\n   142→}\n   143→\n   144→// Add a name/value pair, unless it would collide with the non-empty Overwrite Metadata\n   145→// field. However, with the\n// type-and-unit-label feature (PROM-39), this information can be now stored directly\n// in the special schema metadata labels, which offers better reliability (e.g. atomicity),\n// compatibility and, in many cases, efficiency.\n//\n// NOTE: Metadata in the current form is generally similar (yet different) to:\n//   - The MetricFamily definition in OpenMetrics (https://prometheus.io/docs/specs/om/open_metrics_spec/#metricfamily).\n//     However, there is a small and important distinction around the metric name semantics\n//     for the \"classic\" representation of complex metrics like histograms. The\n//     Metadata.Name follows the __name__ semantics. See Name for details.\n//   - Original metadata.Metadata entries. However, not all fields in that metadata\n//     are \"identifiable\", notably the help field, plus metadata does not contain Name.\ntype Metadata struct {\n\t// Name represents the final metric name for a Prometheus series.\n\t// NOTE(bwplotka): Prometheus scrape formats (e.g. OpenMetrics) define\n\t// the \"metric family name\". The Metadata.Name (so __name__ label) is not\n\t// always the same as the MetricFamily.Name e.g.:\n\t// * OpenMetrics metric family name on scrape: \"acme_http_router_request_seconds\"\n\t// * Resulting Prometheus metric name: \"acme_http_router_request_seconds_sum\"\n\t//\n\t// Empty string means nameless metric (e.g. result of the PromQL function).\n\tName string\n\t// Type represents the metric type. Empty value (\"\") is equivalent to\n\t// model.UnknownMetricType.\n\tType model.MetricType\n\t// Unit represents the metric unit. Empty string means an unitless metric (e.g.\n\t// result of the PromQL function).\n\t//\n\t// NOTE: Currently unit value is not strictly defined other than OpenMetrics\n\t// recommendations: https://prometheus.io/docs/specs/om/open_metrics_spec/#units-and-base-units\n\t// TODO(bwplotka): Consider a stricter validation and rules e.g. lowercase only or UCUM standard.\n\t// Read more in https://github.com/prometheus/proposals/blob/main/proposals/2024-09-25_metadata-labels.md#more-strict-unit-and-type-value-definition\n\tUnit string\n}\n\n// NewMetadataFromLabels returns the schema metadata from the labels.\nfunc NewMetadataFromLabels(ls labels.Labels) Metadata {\n\ttyp := model.MetricTypeUnknown\n\tif got := ls.Get(model.MetricTypeLabel); got != \"\" {\n\t\ttyp = model.MetricType(got)\n\t}\n\treturn Metadata{\n\t\tName: ls.Get(model.MetricNameLabel),\n\t\tType: typ,\n\t\tUnit: ls.Get(model.MetricUnitLabel),\n\t}\n}\n\n// IsTypeEmpty returns true if the metric type is empty (not set).\nfunc (m Metadata) IsTypeEmpty() bool {\n\treturn m.Type == \"\" || m.Type == model.MetricTypeUnknown\n}\n\n// IsEmptyFor returns true if the Metadata field, represented by the given labelName\n// is empty (not set). {\n\t\tb.Add(model.MetricUnitLabel, m.Unit)\n\t}\n}\n\n// SetToLabels injects metric schema metadata as labels into the labels.Builder.\n// It follows the labels.Builder.Set semantics, so empty Metadata fields will\n// remove the corresponding existing labels if they were previously set.\nfunc (m Metadata) SetToLabels(b *labels.Builder) {\n\tb.Set(model.MetricNameLabel, m.Name)\n\tif m.Type == model.MetricTypeUnknown {\n\t\t// Unknown equals empty semantically, so remove the label on unknown too as per\n\t\t// method signature comment.\n\t\tb.Set(model.MetricTypeLabel, \"\")\n\t} else {\n\t\tb.Set(model.MetricTypeLabel, string(m.Type))\n\t}\n\tb.Set(model.MetricUnitLabel, m.Unit)\n}\n\n// NewIgnoreOverriddenMetadataLabelScratchBuilder creates
